Annual Report - General Order No. R5-2007-0035

ADDITIONAL NOTES

A. NOTES

Precipitation utilized to meet freshwater needs of winter forage.

Irrigation Wells IW #201, 225, 231, 239, 254, 256, & 258 were non-operational in 2023. All wells will be sampled once the wells become operational and/or used
during the cropping season. Heavy rains during the winter season allowed for a greater amount of surface water allocation to grow crops.

Fields 209E Winter Forage, 209W Rye Grass, 217 Rye Grass, 218 Rye Grass, 226 Winter Forage, 228 Winter Forage, 233 Winter Forage, 238 Winter Forage,
209W Corn, 216 Corn, 215 Alfalfa, 219 Alfalfa, 221 Alfalfa, 223 Alfalfa, 225 Alfalfa, 227 W Alfalfa & 239 Alfalfa had lower than anticipated removal rates. This
was due to lower than expected yields and/or lower than expected %N. The %N was based on analysis that was derived through a certified laboratory. However,
the applications to these fields matched the low removal rates and was able to meet the field ratio threshold of 1.4.

Field 216 Rye Grass, 220 Rye Grass, 222 Rye Grass, 230 Almonds, 231, Almonds, 235 Almonds, 236 Almonds, & 237 Almonds had lower than anticipated
removal rates, which was due to lower than anticipated %N &/or extremely low tonnage. The low removal rates resulted in field ratios slightly exceeding target
limits, even though application rates did not exceed expected removals.

Almond fields are young trees which led to extremely small removal rates, due to low tonnage & %N. As trees become mature removal rates will increase.
Rye grass fields received initial nutrient applications only. Producer noticed that crop growth was stunted and therefore no additional nutrients were applied.

Nutrients applied to permanent crops, such as trees and vines, are used for tree growth, vine development and fruit production (grapes, nuts, etc.). Comparing
nutrient applications to nutrient content of harvested material for permanent crops is not appropriate and will result in high field ratios. A more accurate reporting
methodology will need to be developed in order to account for nutrients retained in the permanent crops. All applications will continue to be monitored closely to
ensure that over application of nutrients does not occur.

Fields 214 Alfalfa, 215 Alfalfa, 219 Alfalfa, 221 Alfalfa, 223 Alfalfa, 230 Almonds, 231 Almonds, 234 Tomatoes, 235 Almonds, 236 Almonds, 237 Almonds, 238
Tomatoes & 239 Alfalfa received no wastewater or solid manure in 2023. All nutrients applied to these fields were contributed through freshwater applications

and/or commercial fertilizer only.

Fields 227E & 229E were fallow during the winter 2023 cropping season.

Manure/Process Wastewater Tracking Manifests

Corrective Actions Documents

General Order. Deficiencies not corrected in 30 days must be accompanied by an explanation of the factors preventing immediate correction.

General Order, Groundwater Reporting Section starting on page MRP-13.

Storm Water Monitoring

Dischargers that are required to monitor storm water more frequently than required in the General Order must submit monitoring results as directed in the General Order,
Storm Water Reporting Section on page MRP-14.
